The Origin of Souls Must Be from Intellects
Al-Taftazani argues that the proximate principle of all souls cannot be the Necessary Being nor bodies nor souls, but an intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Taftazani's argument that the proximate principle of all souls must be an intellect, and why he acknowledges its dependence on a contested philosophical premise.

Core Idea
The proximate origin of all souls is an intellect, not God or matter.

In this passage, al-Taftazani argues for the philosophical position that the proximate origin of every soul is an intellect—a separate, immaterial substance. He eliminates other candidates: the Necessary Being, bodies, and other souls. However, he also points out that the argument rests on a premise not accepted by all theologians. This lesson walks through his reasoning and its critical flaw.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get a sense of the argument.
Notice the elimination structure: each candidate is rejected with a reason.
2
Identify the four candidates eliminated
The passage eliminates the Necessary Being, bodies, souls, and then applies the same to bodies again. Find each one.
The conclusion is that the intellect is determined.
3
Understand why each is eliminated
For each candidate, note the specific reason given. For the Necessary: because souls are with bodies. For bodies: they act through position. For souls: the question is about the first principle.
4
Note the author's critical remark
Al-Taftazani says some premises are weak, based on the assumption that the Maker is a necessitating agent from whom only one proceeds. This is a key critique.
This connects to the broader debate between theologians and philosophers.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this argument fits into the larger discussion of causality and the relationship between God and creation in Islamic thought.
This prepares you for later lessons on intellects and souls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن مبدأ النفوس كلها من حيث هي نفوس، يجب أن يكون من العقول، إذ لا يجوز أن يكون هو الواجب، لأن النفوس لا تكون إلا مع الأجسام فلا تصدر عن الواحد الحقيقي ولا أن تكون من الأجسام وأجزائها ، وأحوالها، لأنها إنما تفعل بمشاركة الوضع، فلا تؤثر فيما لا وضع له ولا من النفوس لأن الكلام في المبدأ القريب الذي تستند إليه كلية النفوس، وإن كان بعضها من البعض، وبهذا يتبين أن المبدأ القريب لكلية الأجسام لا يجوز أن يكون هو الواجب، ولا الجسم وأجزاؤه وأحواله ولا النفس، لأنها من حيث هي نفس إنما تفعل بواسطة الجسم، فتعين العقل، ولا يخفي ضعف بعض المقدمات وابتنائها على كون الصانع موجباً لا يصدر عنه إلا الواحد.
And among them is that the principle of all souls, insofar as they are souls, must be from the intellects, because it is not permissible that it be the Necessary ( al-wājib ), since souls exist only with bodies, so they cannot proceed from the True One; nor that it be from bodies and their parts and states, because they only act through participation in position ( wadʿ ), so they cannot affect something that has no position; nor from souls, because the discussion is about the proximate principle upon which all souls depend, even if some come from others. By this it becomes clear that the proximate principle of all bodies cannot be the Necessary, nor a body and its parts and states, nor a soul, because it, insofar as it is a soul, only acts through the intermediary of the body. So the intellect is determined, and it is not hidden that some of the premises are weak, based on the assumption that the Maker is an agent of necessitation from whom only one proceeds.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the proximate origin of all souls must be an intellect. The argument proceeds by elimination: the principle ( mabdaʾ ) of souls cannot be the Necessary Being ( al-wājib ), because souls are always associated with bodies, and the True One cannot be the direct source of what is material. It cannot be from bodies or their accidents, because bodies only act through position ( wadʿ ) and thus cannot affect immaterial things. It cannot be from other souls, because the question concerns the first principle on which all souls depend, even if some souls generate others. The same reasoning applies to bodies: their proximate principle cannot be the Necessary, nor a body, nor a soul. Hence, the only remaining candidate is an intellect. The author notes critically that some premises of this argument are weak, being based on the philosophical assumption that the Maker ( al-Ṣāniʿ ) is a necessitating agent from whom only one effect proceeds—a premise not accepted by all theologians.

Key Terms
مبدأ قريب
الواجب
الواحد الحقيقي
وضع
الصانع موجب
تعين العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is definitive and universally accepted.
Correction: The author himself points out that some premises are weak, being based on the contested philosophical assumption that the Maker is a necessitating agent from whom only one proceeds.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that souls cannot proceed directly from the Necessary Being?
A) Because the Necessary Being is one and cannot create many
B) Because souls exist only with bodies, so they cannot issue from the True One
C) Because souls are immaterial
D) Because souls are eternal

Key Takeaway
The argument that souls must originate from an intellect stands on a series of eliminations, but its strength depends on accepting the philosophical premise that the Necessary Being can only produce one effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you accept arguments about God's nature based purely on human reasoning, without checking whether they align with revelation or your own sense of God's majesty? How might this lesson's warning about weak premises challenge you to examine the foundations of your own beliefs?
?
The author says some premises are 'weak' because they assume God must act by necessitation. Have you ever assumed God is limited by your human logic? What would it mean for your worship to truly believe that God's power is beyond all constraints?
?
If the immediate source of your soul is a created intellect, not God directly, does that make you feel further from Him? Or does it call you to reflect on the chain of causes and your complete dependence on the ultimate Creator? How can you live today with deeper awareness of that dependence?

Causality and Created Things

The Emanation Scheme of Intellects, Souls, and Bodies
Al-Taftazani outlines the emanation scheme from the first intellect to the spheres.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' emanation scheme, where from the first intellect proceed an intellect, a soul, and a body, and how this cascade continues to the spheres.

Core Idea
Multiplicity emerges from the One through three aspects of each intellect.

This passage presents the philosophers' elaborate scheme for how the universe proceeds from the One. According to this view, from the first intellect come an intellect, a soul, and a body, and this continues down to the lowest sphere. The scheme attempts to reconcile the unity of the First Cause with the multiplicity of creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the scheme description
Read the Arabic passage slowly, noting how the first intellect is described and what proceeds from it.
The scheme is highly abstract; focus on the three aspects: existence, necessity, possibility.
2
Identify the three aspects
List the three 'considerations' (iʿtibārāt) that cause the emanation: existence, necessity through another, and possibility.
Each aspect yields a different entity: intellect, soul, sphere.
3
Trace the cascade
Realize that the same pattern repeats from the second intellect onward until the last sphere.
The active intellect governs the sublunar world at the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال على ما قيل: إن الصادر الأول عقل، ويصدر عنه باعتبار وجوده عقل، وباعتبار وجوبه بالغير نفس، وباعتبار إمكانه جسم، جرياً على ما هو الأليق، وهكذا إلى الأخير. واعترض بأن تلك الاعتبارات إما وجودية، فيعود المحذور، أو عدمية فلا يصلح أجزاء من الموجد. ولو سلم فلم لا يكفي الواجب لماله من السلوب والإضافات، وكيف يكف الواحد في فلك الثوابت وبأن العقول، إما متفقة الماهية، فلا تنقطع السلسلة، أو لا فيجوز أن لا يحصل الفلك إلا بعد عدة من العقول، فكيف يجزم بأنها عشرة على أن جزئيات الأفلاك فوق التسعة قطعاً، وكلياتها احتمالاً وفي التقصي عن ذلك إطناب لا يليق بالكتاب. إشارة إلى ما ذكره الفلاسفة في ترتيب الوجود، وكيفية صدور النفوس والأجسام عن العقول، وقد سبق أن أول ما يصدر عن الواجب، يجب أن يكون عقلاً، ولا شك أن له وجوداً، وإمكاناً في نفسه، ووجوباً بالغير، وعلماً بذلك وبمبدئه. فقيل صدر عنه باعتبار وجوده عقل وباعتبار وجوبه بالغير نفس، وباعتبار إمكانه فلك إسناداً للأشرف إلى الأشرف. وهكذا من العقل الثاني عقل ونفس وفلك، إلى آخر ما ثبت بالبرهان من وجود الأفلاك، ثم تفويض تدبير عالم العناصر إلى العقل الفعال.
He said, according to what was said: 'The first emanation is an intellect, and from it proceeds, by virtue of its existence, an intellect; by virtue of its necessity through another ( wujūbuhu bi'l-ghayr ), a soul; and by virtue of its possibility ( imkānuhu ), a body, proceeding according to what is most fitting. And so on until the last one.' An objection was raised: 'Those considerations are either existential, then the difficulty returns; or non-existent, then they cannot be parts of the cause. Even if granted, why is the Necessary not sufficient, given that He has negations and relations? And how can the One suffice for the sphere of the fixed stars? And the intellects: either they are identical in quiddity, then the chain would not come to an end; or not, then it is possible that the sphere is not obtained except after several intellects, so how is it certain that they are ten, while the particulars of the spheres are certainly more than nine, and their universals possibly? And in going into that there is prolixity unbecoming of the book.' This is an indication of what the philosophers mentioned in the arrangement of existence and the manner of emanation of souls and bodies from the intellects. It has preceded that the first emanation from the Necessary must be an intellect, and there is no doubt that it has existence, possibility in itself, and necessity through another, and knowledge of that and of its principle. So it was said: from it, by virtue of its existence, proceeds an intellect; by virtue of its necessity through another, a soul; and by virtue of its possibility, a sphere, attributing the nobler to the nobler. And so from the second intellect: intellect, soul, sphere, until the end of what has been established by demonstration of the existence of the spheres. Then the management of the world of elements is delegated to the active intellect.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' famous emanation scheme for the derivation of multiplicity from the One, followed by objections. The scheme holds that from the first intellect (the first emanation) three things proceed: an intellect (by virtue of its existence), a soul (by virtue of its necessity through another), and a body (by virtue of its possibility). This continues down the hierarchy. The objection attacks the coherence of these 'considerations' ( iʿtibārāt ): are they real or mental? If real, the problem of deriving multiplicity from the One remains; if merely mental, they cannot serve as real causes. Further objections: even if accepted, why not suffice with the Necessary's own attributes (negations and relations) to generate multiplicity? How does one sphere derive from the first intellect while there are many spheres? And regarding the number of intellects, there is no proof they are exactly ten. The author then notes that this summary indicates the philosophers' view, reiterating the basic scheme: from the first intellect (which is necessary by another, possible in itself) come three: intellect, soul, sphere ( falk ), continuing until the last sphere, after which the active intellect governs the sublunar world. The author's tone suggests he finds some of these objections valid and the scheme not fully convincing.

وجوب بالغير

فلك
تفويض تدبير

Correction: It is a philosophical view presented here with objections; the author does not endorse it.

Checkpoint

The emanation scheme uses three aspects of each intellect to generate multiplicity from the One.

?
The scheme treats intellects, souls, and bodies as arising from aspects of a single intellect. How does this compare to your understanding of tawhid? Do you see any danger in reducing divine creativity to a mechanical process?

Objections to the Emanation Scheme
Al-Taftazani records several objections against the emanation scheme.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the major objections raised against the philosophers' emanation scheme, particularly the dilemma of the 'considerations' and the uncertainty about the number of intellects.

Core Idea
The emanation scheme fails because its components are either real (contradicting unity) or mental (insufficient as causes).

After presenting the emanation scheme, al-Taftazani records several objections that expose its weaknesses. These objections question the nature of the 'considerations' (iʿtibārāt) that supposedly generate multiplicity, and also challenge the claim that there are exactly ten intellects.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic text containing the objections, noting the structure: dilemmas followed by further problems.
The objections are dense; read slowly and identify each distinct point.
2
Analyze the first objection
The considerations are either existential (real) or non-existent (mental). If real, multiplicity returns as infinite regress; if mental, they cannot cause real entities.
This is a classic dilemma against the scheme.
3
Examine the other objections
Even if the considerations are accepted, why not rely on Allah's own negations and relations? Also, how can one intellect produce the sphere of fixed stars? And the number ten is arbitrary.
These objections attack the scheme's internal logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال على ما قيل: إن الصادر الأول عقل، ويصدر عنه باعتبار وجوده عقل، وباعتبار وجوبه بالغير نفس، وباعتبار إمكانه جسم، جرياً على ما هو الأليق، وهكذا إلى الأخير. واعترض بأن تلك الاعتبارات إما وجودية، فيعود المحذور، أو عدمية فلا يصلح أجزاء من الموجد. ولو سلم فلم لا يكفي الواجب لماله من السلوب والإضافات، وكيف يكف الواحد في فلك الثوابت وبأن العقول، إما متفقة الماهية، فلا تنقطع السلسلة، أو لا فيجوز أن لا يحصل الفلك إلا بعد عدة من العقول، فكيف يجزم بأنها عشرة على أن جزئيات الأفلاك فوق التسعة قطعاً، وكلياتها احتمالاً وفي التقصي عن ذلك إطناب لا يليق بالكتاب. إشارة إلى ما ذكره الفلاسفة في ترتيب الوجود، وكيفية صدور النفوس والأجسام عن العقول، وقد سبق أن أول ما يصدر عن الواجب، يجب أن يكون عقلاً، ولا شك أن له وجوداً، وإمكاناً في نفسه، ووجوباً بالغير، وعلماً بذلك وبمبدئه. فقيل صدر عنه باعتبار وجوده عقل وباعتبار وجوبه بالغير نفس، وباعتبار إمكانه فلك إسناداً للأشرف إلى الأشرف. وهكذا من العقل الثاني عقل ونفس وفلك، إلى آخر ما ثبت بالبرهان من وجود الأفلاك، ثم تفويض تدبير عالم العناصر إلى العقل الفعال.
He said, according to what was said: 'The first emanation is an intellect, and from it proceeds, by virtue of its existence, an intellect; by virtue of its necessity through another ( wujūbuhu bi'l-ghayr ), a soul; and by virtue of its possibility ( imkānuhu ), a body, proceeding according to what is most fitting. And so on until the last one.' An objection was raised: 'Those considerations are either existential, then the difficulty returns; or non-existent, then they cannot be parts of the cause. Even if granted, why is the Necessary not sufficient, given that He has negations and relations? And how can the One suffice for the sphere of the fixed stars? And the intellects: either they are identical in quiddity, then the chain would not come to an end; or not, then it is possible that the sphere is not obtained except after several intellects, so how is it certain that they are ten, while the particulars of the spheres are certainly more than nine, and their universals possibly? And in going into that there is prolixity unbecoming of the book.' This is an indication of what the philosophers mentioned in the arrangement of existence and the manner of emanation of souls and bodies from the intellects. It has preceded that the first emanation from the Necessary must be an intellect, and there is no doubt that it has existence, possibility in itself, and necessity through another, and knowledge of that and of its principle. So it was said: from it, by virtue of its existence, proceeds an intellect; by virtue of its necessity through another, a soul; and by virtue of its possibility, a sphere, attributing the nobler to the nobler. And so from the second intellect: intellect, soul, sphere, until the end of what has been established by demonstration of the existence of the spheres. Then the management of the world of elements is delegated to the active intellect.

This passage presents the philosophers' famous emanation scheme for the derivation of multiplicity from the One, followed by objections. The First Intellect's Aspects and the Objection
States the philosophers' claim and an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' claim that the first intellect has three aspects generating intellect, soul, and body, and the key objection that these aspects either reintroduce multiplicity or cannot be causes.

Core Idea
The first intellect's aspects create a problem of multiplicity that cannot be resolved.

The philosophers propose that the first emanation is an intellect with three aspects, but this leads to logical difficulties. In this passage, the author states the claim and then presents a powerful objection that challenges the coherence of the emanationist model. Let's read the passage and see how the objection unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim
Read the first sentence: the first emanation is an intellect, and from it proceed three things by virtue of three aspects. Note what each aspect produces.
The claim is built on a principle of 'what is most appropriate' (jaryan 'ala ma huwa al-alyaq).
2
Understand the main objection
The objection says the three considerations (existence, necessity, contingency) are either existential or non-existential. Identify why each option is problematic.
3
Examine additional objections
The passage raises further objections: why is the Necessary not sufficient? And how can one be certain of exactly ten intellects given the spheres?
These objections target the internal consistency of the philosophical system.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author dismisses a full pursuit as prolix. Consider why the objections are considered decisive enough to stop further discussion.
This shows the author's confidence that the objections are unanswerable within the philosophers' framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال على ما قيل: إن الصادر الأول عقل، ويصدر عنه باعتبار وجوده عقل، وباعتبار وجوبه بالغير نفس، وباعتبار إمكانه جسم، جرياً على ما هو الأليق، وهكذا إلى الأخير. واعترض بأن تلك الاعتبارات إما وجودية، فيعود المحذور، أو عدمية فلا يصلح أجزاء من الموجد. ولو سلم فلم لا يكفي الواجب لماله من السلوب والإضافات، وكيف يكف الواحد في فلك الثوابت وبأن العقول، إما متفقة الماهية، فلا تنقطع السلسلة، أو لا فيجوز أن لا يحصل الفلك إلا بعد عدة من العقول، فكيف يجزم بأنها عشرة على أن جزئيات الأفلاك فوق التسعة قطعاً، وكلياتها احتمالاً وفي التقصي عن ذلك إطناب لا يليق بالكتاب.
He said, according to what was said: The first emanation is an intellect, and from it proceeds, by virtue of its existence, an intellect; by virtue of its necessity through another, a soul; and by virtue of its contingency, a body – proceeding according to what is most appropriate, and so on to the last. It was objected that those considerations are either existential – thus the difficulty returns – or non-existential, so they cannot be parts of the efficient cause. And even if granted, why is the Necessary not sufficient given what it has of negations and relations? And how can the One suffice for the sphere of the fixed stars? And [it was objected] that the intellects are either of identical essence, then the chain would not terminate, or not, then it is possible that the sphere does not occur except after a number of intellects, so how can one be certain they are ten, given that the particulars of the spheres are definitely more than nine, and their universals possibly so? And pursuing that fully would be a lengthy digression unbefitting of the book.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' view on the first intellect and then an objection to it. The author begins by stating the claim: the first emanation is an intellect, and from it three things proceed by virtue of three aspects – its existence gives an intellect, its necessity through another gives a soul, and its contingency gives a body. This pattern continues. Then an objection is raised: those considerations (existence, necessity, contingency) are either real (existential) or unreal (non-existential). If real, the problem of multiplicity from the One returns; if unreal, they cannot be parts of the efficient cause. Furthermore, even if the aspects are granted, why is the Necessary Being not sufficient? And regarding the spheres, how can one assert exactly ten intellects? The objections highlight inconsistencies in the philosophical system. The author dismisses full pursuit as prolix.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The objection clarifies they are mere considerations (i'tibarāt). If they were real, multiplicity returns; if not real, they cannot be causes.

Checkpoint

Emanation of Intellects, Souls, and Spheres
Philosophers' emanation scheme of intellects, souls, spheres

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' account of how intellects, souls, and spheres emanate from the First Intellect.

Core Idea
The first emanation is an intellect, which then emanates intellect, soul, and sphere from its aspects.

This passage presents the philosophers' hierarchical emanation scheme, beginning with the first intellect that emanates from the Necessary. It explains how three distinct realities—intellect, soul, and sphere—proceed from each subsequent intellect, down to the celestial spheres. The passage also offers an alternative view on the first intellect's emanations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overview of the emanation scheme.
2
Identify the three aspects of the first intellect
Notice that the first intellect has existence, necessity by another, and contingency. From these emanate intellect, soul, and sphere respectively.
This is the standard view.
3
Understand the hierarchy
Each subsequent intellect similarly emanates an intellect, soul, and sphere until the last sphere.
The management of the elemental world is given to the last intellect.
4
Examine the alternative view
The passage also mentions another perspective: from the first intellect, by virtue of its contingency, matter; existence, form; knowledge, intellect; and knowledge of cause, soul.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this emanation scheme relates to divine transcendence and causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إشارة إلى ما ذكره الفلاسفة في ترتيب الوجود، وكيفية صدور النفوس والأجسام عن العقول، وقد سبق أن أول ما يصدر عن الواجب، يجب أن يكون عقلاً، ولا شك أن له وجوداً، وإمكاناً في نفسه، ووجوباً بالغير، وعلماً بذلك وبمبدئه. فقيل صدر عنه باعتبار وجوده عقل وباعتبار وجوبه بالغير نفس، وباعتبار إمكانه فلك إسناداً للأشرف إلى الأشرف. وهكذا من العقل الثاني عقل ونفس وفلك، إلى آخر ما ثبت بالبرهان من وجود الأفلاك، ثم تفويض تدبير عالم العناصر إلى العقل الأخير بمعونة الأوضاع والحركات وقيل صدر عن العقل الأول باعتبار إمكانه هيولي الفلك الأعظم، وباعتبار وجوده صورته وباعتبار علمه بوجوب وجوده بعلته عقله وباعتبار علمه بعلته نفسه.
Reference to what the philosophers mentioned about the order of existence and the manner of emanation of souls and bodies from the intellects. It has preceded that the first thing that emanates from the Necessary must be an intellect; there is no doubt that it has existence, contingency in itself, necessity through another, and knowledge of that and of its principle. So it was said: from it emanates, by virtue of its existence, an intellect; by virtue of its necessity through another, a soul; and by virtue of its contingency, a sphere – attributing the nobler to the nobler. And likewise from the second intellect an intellect, a soul, and a sphere, up to the last of what has been established by proof of the existence of spheres, then entrusting the management of the world of elements to the last intellect with the aid of positions and motions. And it was said: from the first intellect emanates, by virtue of its contingency, the matter of the greatest sphere; by virtue of its existence, its form; by virtue of its knowledge of its existence being necessary through its cause, its intellect; and by virtue of its knowledge of its cause, its soul.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the philosophers' emanation scheme. It begins by recalling that the first emanation from the Necessary must be an intellect, which has existence, contingency, necessity by another, and knowledge. From this intellect three things emanate: by virtue of its existence, an intellect; by virtue of its necessity by another, a soul; by virtue of its contingency, a sphere. This hierarchy continues down to the last sphere. Then the management of the elemental world is delegated to the last intellect. An alternative view is also given: from the first intellect emanate the matter of the greatest sphere (by contingency), its form (by existence), its intellect (by knowledge of its necessary existence through its cause), and its soul (by knowledge of its cause).

Philosophical Solution to Multiplicity from the One
Presents the philosophical argument for multiplicity from the One using i'tibarat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical argument for how multiplicity can emanate from the One without compromising its unity, and the role of 'considerations and aspects' (i'tibarat) in that scheme.

Core Idea
Multiplicity from the One is explained by aspects, not independent causes.

In this passage, the author presents the philosophers' proposed solution to the problem of how the many can proceed from the truly One. They argue that concepts like existence and contingency are not separate causes but rather aspects (i'tibarat) that differentiate the states of efficient causes. This allows for a chain of emanations without introducing multiplicity into the First Principle. The passage cites Ibn Sina's al-Shifa and discusses the intellects and the refutation of objections, though the text cuts off mid-sentence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage straight through. Then read the full translation. Notice the flow: the problem statement, the solution via i'tibarat, the citation from al-Shifa, the discussion of intellects, and the beginning of objections.
The passage ends abruptly; the first objection is incomplete.
2
Focus on the concept of i'tibarat
Identify how the philosophers treat existence, necessity, and contingency. They are not independent causes but 'considerations and aspects' that affect how causes produce effects. This is key to preserving the unity of the First Cause.
Compare this to the view of independent causes, which would imply multiplicity in the One.
3
Trace the chain of intellects
The passage explains that intellects are not all of the same species, so their effects can vary. A chain is possible down to the material world. The Necessary Being, on the other hand, has no multiplicity of aspects.
The philosophers did not fix the number of intellects or their aspects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه لما ثبت عندهم امتناع صدور الكثير عن الواحد الحقيقي، ذكروا طريقاً في صدور الكثرة عن الواحد، على أنه احتمال راجح في نظرهم من غير قطع به، ولم يجعلوا الوجود والإمكان ونحو ذلك عللاً مستقلة، بل اعتبارات وحيثيات تختلف بها أحوال العلل الموجدة على ما قال في الشفاء نحن لا نمنع أن يكون عن شيء واحد، ذات واحدة، ثم يتبعها كثرة إضافية، ليست في أول وجودها داخلة في مبدأ قوامها، بل يجوز أن يكون الواحد يلزم عنه واحد ثم ذلك الواحد يلزمه حكم أو حال أو صفة أو معلول، ويكون ذلك أيضاً واحداً، ثم يلزم عنه لذاته شيء، وبمشاركة ذلك اللازم شيء، فتنبع من العلة هناك كثرة كلها تلزم ذاته، فيجب أن يكون مثل هذه الكثرة هي لإمكان وجود الكثرة معاً عن المعلولات الأولى، ثم العقول ليست متفقة الأنواع، حتى يلزم اتفاق آثارها بأن يصدر عن كل منها عقل ونفس وفلك. بل يجوز سلسلة العقول إلى ما يكون مبدأ الهيولي العناصر، وما يعرض لها من الصور والأعراض، بحسب ما له من الحيثيات وما يحصل للمواد من الاستعدادات، بخلاف الواجب، فإنه ليس فيه كثرة حيثيات واعتبارات، وأما السلوب والإضافات فإنما تعقل بعد ثبوت الغير فلو علل ثبوت الغير بها كان دوراً، ولم يقطعوا بأن العقول ليست فوق العشرة، وأن حيثيات كل عقل تنحصر في الثلاث أو الأربع، فلا يمتنع أن يكون مبدأ فلك الثوابت عقولاً كثيرة، أو عقلا واحداً، باعتبارات وحيثيات غير محصورة وبما ذكر يندفع اعتراضات : الأول: أن الوجود والوجوب والإمكان إن كانت أموراً اعتبارية لا تحقق لها في
Know that when it was established for them that the emanation of multiplicity from the truly One is impossible, they mentioned a way for the emanation of multiplicity from the One, as a preponderant probability in their view without certainty. They did not treat existence, contingency, and the like as independent causes, but rather as considerations and aspects by which the states of the efficient causes differ. According to what is said in al-Shifa: we do not deny that from one thing, one essence, there may follow an additional multiplicity not entering into the principle of its subsistence at the beginning of its existence. Rather it is possible that from the one something one follows, then that one is followed by a judgment, state, attribute, or effect, and that too is one; then from it something follows by its essence, and by participation with that consequent something [else], so from the cause there emerges a multiplicity all of which follow from its essence. So such multiplicity must be for the possibility of the existence of multiplicity together from the first effects. Moreover, the intellects are not all of the same species such that their effects would be uniform – that from each an intellect, a soul, and a sphere emanate. Rather a chain of intellects is possible up to what becomes the principle of the matter of the elements and what occurs to them of forms and accidents, according to its aspects and the dispositions acquired by the materials. This differs from the Necessary, in whom there is no multiplicity of aspects and considerations. As for negations and relations, they are only understood after the existence of another; if one were to cause the existence of another by them, it would be circular. They did not assert that the intellects are not more than ten, or that the aspects of each intellect are limited to three or four. Hence it is not impossible that the principle of the sphere of fixed stars be many intellects, or one intellect with unlimited aspects and considerations. By what has been mentioned, objections are refuted: First, that existence, necessity, and contingency, if they are merely relative matters having no reality in…
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' solution to the problem of how multiplicity can proceed from the truly One. The author explains that philosophers considered existence, contingency, etc. not as separate causes but as aspects (i’tibarat) that differentiate the states of causes. Citing Ibn Sina's al-Shifa, the argument states that from one thing can follow a multiplicity of judgments, states, attributes, or effects without breaking the unity of the first cause. The intellects are not uniform in species, so their emanations can vary, and a chain is possible leading to the material world. The Necessary Being has no multiplicity of aspects, but negations and relations are not causes. The philosophers did not fix the number of intellects or their aspects. The passage then begins to list objections, the first being that if existence, necessity, and contingency are merely relative, they have no reality… but the text ends mid-sentence.

Correction: The author clarifies that the scheme is only a preponderant probability (ihtimal rajih) in their view, not a certainty (qat').

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how did the philosophers treat existence, contingency, and similar concepts in explaining multiplicity from the One?

B) As considerations and aspects

Key Takeaway
The philosophical solution uses 'considerations' to avoid independent causes, allowing multiplicity from the One without certainty.

How can you train your heart to worship a God beyond all composition, and will you let this truth transform your prayer from a list of requests into pure awe?
?

?

How does this realization hit you — does it make you feel fragile or freed? And what will you do today to live as someone who truly depends on God alone?

The Emanation Scheme: From One to Many via Aspects
Describes the basic emanation scheme and the role of aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the philosophers used aspects (haythiyyat) to explain the emergence of multiplicity from a single First Intellect without violating the principle 'from one only one proceeds'.

Core Idea
Multiplicity emerges from the One through aspects, not independent causes.

The philosophers faced a dilemma: how can the many exist if only One is the source? They devised a scheme where a single cause can produce multiple effects by considering different aspects of that cause. In this lesson, we see the basic structure of that scheme, beginning with the First Intellect and the quote from Ibn Sina's Shifa explaining how a single essence can have accidental multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the First Intellect's aspects
Carefully read the opening sentences describing how the supreme sphere's matter, form, intellect, and self originate from the first intellect through different considerations.
Notice the four distinct aspects: potentiality, existence, knowledge of its cause, knowledge of its own necessity.
2
Grasp the principle and the use of aspects
Understand the key principle: the philosophers deny that existence and potentiality are independent causes; they are mere considerations that vary the states of efficient causes.
This is their solution to the 'one from one' problem.
3
Analyze Ibn Sina's Shifa quotation
Read the quotation carefully to see how a single essence can generate a chain of consequences, each one leading to the next, resulting in multiplicity.
The quote illustrates that multiplicity is accidental and follows from the essence, not from multiple independent principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأخير بمعونة الأوضاع والحركات وقيل صدر عن العقل الأول باعتبار إمكانه هيولي الفلك الأعظم، وباعتبار وجوده صورته وباعتبار علمه بوجوب وجوده بعلته عقله وباعتبار علمه بعلته نفسه واعلم أنه لما ثبت عندهم امتناع صدور الكثير عن الواحد الحقيقي، ذكروا طريقاً في صدور الكثرة عن الواحد، على أنه احتمال راجح في نظرهم من غير قطع به، ولم يجعلوا الوجود والإمكان ونحو ذلك علللا مستقلة، بل اعتبارات وحيثيات تختلف بها أحوال العلل الموجدة على ما قال في الشفاء نحن لا نمنع أن يكون عن شيء واحد، ذات واحدة، ثم يتبعها كثرة إضافية، ليست في أول وجودها داخلة في مبدأ قوامها، بل يجوز أن يكون الواحد يلزم عنه واحد ثم ذلك الواحد يلزمه حكم أو حال أو صفة أو معلول، ويكون ذلك أيضاً واحداً، ثم يلزم عنه لذاته شيء، وبمشاركة ذلك اللازم شيء، فتنبع من العلة هناك كثرة كلها تلزم ذاته، فيجب أن يكون مثل هذه الكثرة هي لإمكان وجود الكثرة معاً عن المعلولات الأولى، ثم العقول ليست متفقة الأنواع، حتى يلزم (٣) اتفاق (٤)، آثارها بأن يصدر عن كل منها عقل ونفس، وفلك. بل يجوز سلسلة العقول إلى ما يكون مبدأ الهيولي العناصر، وما يعرض لها من الصور والأعراض، بحسب ما له من الحيثيات وما يحصل للمواد من الاستعدادات، بخلاف الواجب، فإنه ليس فيه كثرة حيثيات واعتبارات، وأما السلوب والإضافات فإنما تعقل بعد ثبوت الغير فلو علل ثبوت الغير بها كان دوراً، ولم يقطعوا بأن العقول ليست فوق العشرة، وأن حيثيات كل عقل تنحصر في الثلاث أو الأربع، فلا يمتنع أن يكون مبدأ فلك الثوابت عقولاً كثيرة، أو عقلا واحداً، باعتبارات وحيثيات غير محصورة وبما ذكر يندفع اعتراضات :
The last [intellect] with the aid of positions and motions, and it was said that it originated from the first intellect in consideration of its potentiality [as] the matter of the supreme sphere, and in consideration of its existence [as] its form, and in consideration of its knowledge of the necessity of its existence by its cause [as] its intellect, and in consideration of its knowledge of its cause [as] its self. Know that since it is established with them that the emanation of the many from the single True One is impossible, they mentioned a way for the emanation of multiplicity from the One, as a preponderant probability in their view without certainty. They did not make existence, potentiality, and the like independent causes, but rather considerations and aspects by which the states of the efficient causes vary, according to what was said in the Shifa: 'We do not deny that from one thing, one essence, there may follow an accidental multiplicity, not entering into the principle of its constitution at the beginning of its existence. Rather, it is permissible that the one gives rise to a one, then that one gives rise to a judgment, or state, or attribute, or effect, and that is also one, then there arises from it by its essence something, and by the participation of that necessary something, so from the cause there emanates a multiplicity all of which follow from its essence. So such multiplicity must be for the possibility of the existence of multiplicity together from the first effects.' Then the intellects are not of the same species, such that their effects would necessarily agree: that from each should issue an intellect, a soul, and a sphere. Rather, a chain of intellects is possible up to what is the principle of the matter of the elements and what occurs to them of forms and accidents, according to its aspects and the preparations that occur in the materials. Unlike the Necessary [Existence], for there is no multiplicity of aspects and considerations in Him. As for negations and relations, they are only conceived after the establishment of the other. So if the establishment of the other were caused by them, it would be circular. And they did not assert that the intellects are not above ten, nor that the aspects of each intellect are limited to three or four. So it is not impossible that the principle of the sphere of the fixed stars be many intellects, or one intellect, by unlimited considerations and aspects. And by what has been mentioned, objections are repelled:
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage describes the Neoplatonic emanation scheme as proposed by the philosophers (falasifa) to explain how multiplicity can arise from the One, given the principle 'from one only one proceeds'. The author explains that the philosophers consider this scheme as a preponderant probability, not a certainty. They do not take existence and potentiality as independent causes, but as considerations (i'tibarat) and aspects (haythiyyat) that vary the states of the efficient causes. A quote from Ibn Sina's Shifa illustrates that a single essence can have accidental multiplicity through successive consequences. The passage then notes that the intellects are not all of the same species, so their effects differ; a chain is possible up to the material elements. Unlike God, the intellects have multiple aspects. Negations and relations are not grounds for causing existence. The philosophers did not fix the number of intellects or aspects, leaving open possibilities. The passage ends by saying that with this, the following objections are repelled.

The Flexibility of the Emanation Scheme
Discusses the flexibility of the emanation scheme: intellects, aspects, and causal limits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the emanation scheme is not rigid: the intellects are not fixed in number or species, and aspects are not limited, making the scheme open-ended.

Core Idea
The philosophers left the emanation scheme flexible, not asserting fixed numbers.

After presenting the basic emanation scheme, the author addresses potential objections and clarifies that the philosophers did not dogmatically fix the number of intellects or aspects. This lesson explores the flexible nature of the scheme, allowing for a chain of intellects down to the material world, and refuting the idea that negations or relations can be causes.

Guided Path
1
Understand that intellects are not all of the same species
Read that the intellects are not of one species, so their effects vary – they do not all produce the same triad of intellect, soul, and sphere.
2
Learn about the possible chain of intellects
Note that the chain can extend down to the principle of elemental matter, depending on aspects and material preparations.
3
Grasp the limits: negations and relations are not causal
The text states that negations and relations are conceived only after the other is established, so they cannot cause the other – that would be circular.
4
See the open-endedness regarding number and aspects
The philosophers did not assert that the intellects are limited to ten or that aspects are only three or four; many possibilities remain open.
This shows the scheme is not a closed system.

Six Objections to the Emanation Scheme
Lists six objections challenging the emanation scheme's coherence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six major objections that challenge the coherence of the emanation scheme as presented by the philosophers.

Core Idea
The emanation scheme faces multiple logical inconsistencies that undermine its claim to rational necessity.

The emanation scheme attempts to explain the multiplicity of the universe from a single First Principle. However, it is vulnerable to several objections that expose internal contradictions or untenable assumptions. In this passage, the author enumerates six such objections, each targeting a different aspect of the scheme. Understanding these objections is crucial for evaluating the philosophical arguments about causality and emanation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify each objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note that there are six distinct objections, each introduced by ordinal numbers (first, second, etc.).
The objections are presented as arguments against the philosophers' emanation scheme, not as the author's own views.
2
For each objection, note the logical flaw it points to
Go through each objection one by one. Identify what aspect of the emanation scheme is being criticized and why the objection is considered damaging.
3
Consider how these objections collectively weaken the emanation scheme
Think about how the objections fit together. They target different parts of the scheme: the nature of causality, infinite regress, rhetorical principles, multiplicity from unity, and the structure of intellects.
4
Reflect on the implications for the principle 'from one only one'
Many objections directly or indirectly challenge the principle that from one simple cause only one effect can proceed. Consider how each objection relates to this principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول: أن الوجود والوجوب والإمكان إن كانت أموراً اعتبارية لا تحقق لها في الأعيان لم تصلح أجزاء من العلة الموجدة، وإن كانت وجودية متحققة فسواء صدرت عن الواجب أو عن العقل، لزم كون الواحد مصدراً لأكثر من الواحد، وكذا لو جعلنا جهات كثرة العقل تعقله للوجوب ونحوه . الثاني : أنه يلزم على ما ذكر أن يصدر عن كل عقل فلك ونفس وعقل إلى ما لا يتناهى، فلا تنحصر العقول في عدد فضلاً عن العشرة. الثالث: أن حديث إسناد الأشرف إلى الأشرف خطابي لا يليق بالعلوم البرهانية . الرابع: أن إسناد فلك الثوابت مع كثرتها إلى العقل الثاني باعتبار إمكانه يثبت صدور الكثير عن الواحد، وكذا إسناد الصور والأعراض العنصرية إلى العقل الأخير. الخامس : أنه لو كانت الحيثيات العدمية والاعتبارية كافية في صدور الكثير عن الواحد لجاز اسناده إلى الواجب باعتبار ما له من السلوب والإضافات . السادس : أنه إذا كانت العقول مختلفة بالنوع حتى كان الأخير مما تنقطع عنده سلسلة العقول والأفلاك، بأن لا يصدر عنه فلك وعقل، ونفس، جاز في جانب الابتداء أن لا يصدر عن العقل الأول إلا عقل ثان وعن الثاني، إلا عقل ثالث ،وهكذا، حتى يكون صدور الفلك الأعظم بعد صدور عقول كثيرة، وحينئذ لا يصح الجزم بأنه يصدر عن العقل الأول فلك وعقل، ونفس، وبأن العقول عشرة على عدد الأفلاك .
First: that existence, necessity, and potentiality – if they are mental considerations having no reality in external objects, then they are not fit to be parts of the efficient cause; and if they are existential realities, then whether they originate from the Necessary or from the intellect, it follows that the one is the source of more than one, and likewise if we make the directions of the multiplicity of the intellect its intellection of necessity and the like. Second: that it follows from what was mentioned that from each intellect there should issue a sphere, a soul, and an intellect ad infinitum, so the intellects would not be limited in number, let alone to ten. Third: that the saying 'assigning the noblest to the noblest' is rhetorical and not befitting demonstrative sciences. Fourth: that the assignment of the sphere of the fixed stars with their multiplicity to the second intellect in consideration of its potentiality proves the emanation of the many from the one, and likewise the assignment of elemental forms and accidents to the last intellect. Fifth: that if non-existent and mental aspects were sufficient for the emanation of the many from the one, then it would be permissible to ascribe it to the Necessary in consideration of His negations and relations. Sixth: that if the intellects are different in species such that the last of them is where the chain of intellects and spheres ends, in that no sphere, intellect, and soul issue from it, then it is possible at the beginning that from the first intellect only a second intellect issues, and from the second only a third, and so on, until the emanation of the supreme sphere occurs after the emanation of many intellects. In that case, it is not correct to be certain that from the first intellect issues a sphere, an intellect, and a soul, and that the intellects are ten according to the number of spheres.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage lists six specific objections to the philosophers' emanation scheme. First objection: if existence, necessity, and potentiality are merely mental considerations with no external reality, they cannot serve as parts of an efficient cause; but if they are real, then the One would produce multiple things, breaking the 'from one only one' principle. Second objection: the scheme implies an infinite regress of intellects and spheres, so the number cannot be limited to ten. Third objection: the principle of assigning the noblest effect to the noblest cause is rhetorical, not demonstrative. Fourth objection: assigning the sphere of the fixed stars (which contains many stars) to the second intellect via its potentiality actually proves multiplicity from one, contradicting the principle. Fifth objection: if non-existent and mental aspects sufficed, then one could attribute multiplicity directly to God via His negations and relations, which the philosophers deny. Sixth objection: if the last intellect does not produce a sphere, then it is possible that the chain does not start with a sphere from the first intellect, undermining the fixed scheme of ten intellects. Each objection targets a weak point in the emanationist argument.

Key Terms
الوجود
الوجوب
الإمكان
اعتبارية
الحيثيات العدمية
السلوب والإضافات
العلة الموجدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These objections represent the author's own positive doctrine.
Correction: The objections are presented as critiques of the philosophers' emanation scheme, not as the author's own positive assertions.

Checkpoint
According to the third objection, what is criticized about the principle 'assigning the noblest to the noblest'?
A) It is a philosophical truth
B) It is a revealed principle
C) It is rhetorical and not demonstrative
D) It is mathematically proven

Key Takeaway
The six objections collectively undermine the emanation scheme by showing it leads to infinite regress, relies on rhetorical principles, fails to maintain the 'one from one' rule, and allows for alternative structures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the first objection, does it unsettle you to realize that a widely accepted philosophical system can be dismantled by logical scrutiny? In your own faith, are there teachings you accept without examining their logical foundations? Will you commit to examining at least one such teaching this week with the same rigor?
?
The third objection dismisses rhetorical arguments in demonstrative sciences. Where in your life do you rely on emotional rhetoric rather than honest reasoning about your beliefs? What would it cost you to replace that with intellectual honesty?
?
The sixth objection shows that the emanation scheme could have started differently, undermining its certainty. Reflect on a belief you hold with certainty about God’s actions. What would it mean for you if that belief were based on assumptions that could have been otherwise? Will you pray for the courage to question it?

Objection 1: The Intellect's Aspects Cause Multiplicity
First objection: aspects of the Intellect cause multiplicity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection: if the aspects of the First Intellect are real existents, the One becomes a source for more than one, violating the core principle.

Core Idea
If the Intellect's aspects are real, the One produces many.

The philosophers claim that from the One only one can proceed. But their own model gives the First Intellect multiple aspects—its intellection of the Necessary Being, of itself, and of its own possibility. Sanusi argues that if these aspects are actual existents, then whether they emanate from the Necessary Being or from the Intellect, the principle is violated. This objection strikes at the very foundation of the emanation theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the First Objection
Read the Arabic and translation for the first objection. Notice how Sanusi presents a dilemma: either the aspects are real or they are not.
This targets the internal consistency of the emanation theory.
2
Understand the Dilemma
If the aspects (e.g., intellection of necessity) are actual existents, then from the One more than one proceeds. If they are not real, the Intellect's multiplicity is not real, undermining the basis for emanation.
3
Connect to the Principle
Reflect: How does this objection show that the principle 'from one only one proceeds' is violated even at the first step?
The core idea: the Intellect's multiplicity forces the One to produce many.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأعيان لم تصلح أجزاء من العلة الموجدة، وإن كانت وجودية متحققة فسواء صدرت عن الواجب أو عن العقل، لزم كون الواحد مصدراً لأكثر من الواحد، وكذا لو جعلنا جهات كثرة العقل تعقله للوجوب ونحوه. الثاني: أنه يلزم على ما ذكر أن يصدر عن كل عقل فلك ونفس وعقل إلى ما لا يتناهى، فلا تنحصر العقول في عدد فضلاً عن العشرة. الثالث: أن حديث إسناد الأشرف إلى الأشرف خطابي لا يليق بالعلوم البرهانية. الرابع: أن إسناد فلك الثوابت مع كثرتها إلى العقل الثاني باعتبار إمكانه يثبت صدور الكثير عن الواحد، وكذا إسناد الصور والأعراض العنصرية إلى العقل الأخير. الخامس: أنه لو كانت الحيثيات العدمية والاعتبارية كافية في صدور الكثير عن الواحد لجاز اسناده إلى الواجب باعتبار ما له من السلوب والإضافات. السادس: أنه إذا كانت العقول مختلفة بالنوع حتى كان الأخير مما تنقطع عنده سلسلة العقول والأفلاك، بأن لا يصدر عنه فلك وعقل ونفس، جاز في جانب الابتداء أن لا يصدر عن العقل الأول إلا عقل ثان وعن الثاني إلا عقل ثالث وهكذا، حتى يكون صدور الفلك الأعظم بعد صدور عقول كثيرة، وحينئذ لا يصح الجزم بأنه يصدر عن العقل الأول فلك وعقل ونفس، وبأن العقول عشرة على عدد الأفلاك. الأول كيف والأفلاك الجزئية كثيرة يستدعي كل منها مبدأ. واعترفوا بأنه يحتمل أن يكون بين الفلك الأعظم وفلك الثوابت أفلاك كثيرة، وأن يكون كل من الثوابت على فلك هذا، ولا يخفى أن كلامهم في هذا المقام مع ابتنائه على أن الواحد لا يصدر عنه إلا الواحد يشتمل على مقدمات أخر ضعيفة، وأن الاحتمال والأولوية لا يجدي كثير نفع في المطالب العلمية.
The individual entities are not fit to be parts of the efficient cause; and if they are actual existents, then whether they emanate from the Necessary Being or from the Intellect, it necessarily follows that the One is a source for more than one; likewise if we make the aspects of the Intellect's multiplicity its intellection of necessity and the like. Second: It necessarily follows from what was mentioned that from each intellect there emanates a sphere, a soul, and an intellect ad infinitum, so the intellects are not confined to a number, let alone ten. Third: The statement that the nobler is attributed to the nobler is rhetorical, not befitting demonstrative sciences. Fourth: Attributing the sphere of the fixed stars, despite their multiplicity, to the second intellect by virtue of its possibility establishes the emanation of many from the One; likewise attributing elemental forms and accidents to the last intellect. Fifth: If non-existent aspects and relational aspects were sufficient for the emanation of many from the One, then it would be permissible to attribute it to the Necessary Being by virtue of His negations and relations. Sixth: If the intellects differ in species such that the last is one at which the chain of intellects and spheres terminates—in that no sphere, intellect, or soul emanates from it—then it is possible at the beginning that from the first intellect only a second intellect emanates, and from the second only a third, and so on, until the emanation of the greatest sphere occurs after the emanation of many intellects. In that case, it cannot be definitively asserted that from the first intellect there emanates a sphere, an intellect, and a soul, and that the intellects are ten corresponding to the number of spheres. Moreover, how [can it be] when the partial spheres are many, each requiring a principle? And they admitted that it is possible that between the greatest sphere and the sphere of the fixed stars there are many spheres, and that each of the fixed stars has its own sphere. It is not hidden that their discourse in this context—while founded on the principle that from the One only one proceeds—includes other weak premises, and that probability and preference are of little use in scientific inquiries.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents six objections against the philosophers' theory of emanation, specifically against the principle 'from the One only one proceeds'. The objections are enumerated (second through sixth, with the first being implicit in the opening sentence). Each objection highlights a different logical flaw in the emanationist framework: the impossibility of multiplicity arising from a simple One, the infinite regress of intellects, the rhetorical nature of their assumptions, the inconsistency in attributing multiplicity to lower intellects while denying it to the First, the sufficiency of negations and relations in the Necessary Being, and the arbitrary assumption that the chain ends at ten intellects. The passage concludes by noting that the entire discourse rests on weak premises and that mere probability is insufficient for certain knowledge.

العقل
الجهات
الوجوب

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The aspects of the Intellect are merely conceptual and do not cause multiplicity.
Correction: Sanusi argues that if they are real existents, they cause multiplicity; if not, the emanation lacks basis.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi argue about the aspects of the Intellect in the first objection?
A) They are non-existent.
B) If real, they cause the One to produce many.
C) They are parts of the efficient cause.
D) They are only in the Necessary Being.

Key Takeaway
The first objection shows that the philosophers' own account of the First Intellect's multiplicity violates the principle that from one only one proceeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

This passage shows that even intellectual aspects can have real metaphysical consequences. How might your casual theological reasoning be introducing hidden multiplicity into your understanding of Allah's oneness?
?
The objection exposes the failure of relying solely on human intellect to deduce truths about the divine. In what area of your faith are you trusting your own reasoning over revelation? What step can you take today to submit your intellect to the Quran and Sunnah?

Objection 2: Infinite Regress of Intellects
Second objection: infinite regress of intellects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection: if each intellect produces a sphere, soul, and intellect ad infinitum, the intellects are not limited to ten.

Core Idea
The emanation chain leads to infinite intellects, not ten.

The philosophers claim that the chain of intellects ends at ten, corresponding to the spheres. Sanusi points out that if each intellect necessarily produces another intellect along with a sphere and a soul, then the chain would continue forever, contradicting the finite number they assert. This objection exposes an arbitrary stop in their system.

Guided Path
1
Read the Second Objection
Read the Arabic and translation. Mark the key claim: 'from each intellect there emanates a sphere, a soul, and an intellect ad infinitum.'
This is a direct consequence of their own emanation rules.
2
Analyze the Infinite Regress
If each intellect gives rise to another, the series is endless. There is no reason to stop at ten.
3
Consider the Contradiction
The philosophers' system requires a finite number of spheres, but their own principle forces an infinite chain. This is a logical inconsistency.
Sanusi says 'so the intellects are not confined to a number, let alone ten.'

Objection 3: Rhetorical Principle Not Demonstrative
Third objection: rhetorical principle invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection: the principle 'the nobler is attributed to the nobler' is rhetorical, not suitable for demonstrative science.

Core Idea
Rhetoric is not proof; the principle is not demonstrative.

The philosophers often argue that since the First Intellect is nobler, it must produce a nobler effect. Sanusi dismisses this as a rhetorical appeal, not a logical proof. In demonstrative sciences, arguments must be based on necessary premises, not persuasive but uncertain claims. This objection challenges the methodological soundness of the emanation theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the Third Objection
Read the short Arabic sentence. Note the words 'khatabi' (rhetorical) and 'burhaniyya' (demonstrative).
This objection is brief but powerful.
2
Distinguish Rhetoric from Demonstration
Sanusi asserts that the principle 'attributing the nobler to the nobler' is merely rhetorical. In demonstrative sciences, arguments must be certain and based on necessary causal connections, not mere prestige.
3
Apply to the Emanation Theory
The philosophers use this principle to justify the order of emanation. Sanusi says this is not a valid proof; it does not meet the standards of demonstrative science.
This undermines the entire edifice if the key premise is non-demonstrative.

Objection 4: Multiplicity from Lower Intellects
Fourth objection: lower intellects produce many, contradicting principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth objection: if lower intellects can produce multiplicity (e.g., the fixed stars), then the One can as well, contradicting the principle.

Core Idea
Lower intellects produce many, so why not the One?

The philosophers attribute the many fixed stars to the second intellect by virtue of its possibility. But if possibility allows a single intellect to produce many, then the same should apply to the First Intellect or even the Necessary Being. This objection highlights an inconsistency: they allow multiplicity at lower levels but deny it at the top.

Guided Path
1
Read the Fourth Objection
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the key phrase: 'by virtue of its possibility' (bi i'tibari imkanihi).
This is the basis for the objection.
2
Understand the Argument
The philosophers say the second intellect produces the sphere of fixed stars (many stars) because of its possibility. But if possibility can cause multiplicity, then the First Intellect or the Necessary Being, which also have possibility (or negations/relations), should also produce multiplicity. This violates the principle.
3
See the Inconsistency
Sanusi points out that the same logic used for lower intellects would apply to higher ones. Thus the principle 'from one only one proceeds' is not consistently applied.
Also mentions elemental forms and accidents from the last intellect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأعيان لم تصلح أجزاء من العلة الموجدة، وإن كانت وجودية متحققة فسواء صدرت عن الواجب أو عن العقل، لزم كون الواحد مصدراً لأكثر من الواحد، وكذا لو جعلنا جهات كثرة العقل تعقله للوجوب ونحوه. الثاني: أنه يلزم على ما ذكر أن يصدر عن كل عقل فلك ونفس وعقل إلى ما لا يتناهى، فلا تنحصر العقول في عدد فضلاً عن العشرة. الثالث: أن حديث إسناد الأشرف إلى الأشرف خطابي لا يليق بالعلوم البرهانية. الرابع: أن إسناد فلك الثوابت مع كثرتها إلى العقل الثاني باعتبار إمكانه يثبت صدور الكثير عن الواحد، وكذا إسناد الصور والأعراض العنصرية إلى العقل الأخير. الخامس: أنه لو كانت الحيثيات العدمية والاعتبارية كافية في صدور الكثير عن الواحد لجاز اسناده إلى الواجب باعتبار ما له من السلوب والإضافات. السادس: أنه إذا كانت العقول مختلفة بالنوع حتى كان الأخير مما تنقطع عنده سلسلة العقول والأفلاك، بأن لا يصدر عنه فلك وعقل ونفس، جاز في جانب الابتداء أن لا يصدر عن العقل الأول إلا عقل ثان وعن الثاني إلا عقل ثالث وهكذا، حتى يكون صدور الفلك الأعظم بعد صدور عقول كثيرة، وحينئذ لا يصح الجزم بأنه يصدر عن العقل الأول فلك وعقل ونفس، وبأن العقول عشرة على عدد الأفلاك. الأول كيف والأفلاك الجزئية كثيرة يستدعي كل منها مبدأ. واعترفوا بأنه يحتمل أن يكون بين الفلك الأعظم وفلك الثوابت أفلاك كثيرة، وأن يكون كل من الثوابت على فلك هذا، ولا يخفى أن كلامهم في هذا المقام مع ابتنائه على أن الواحد لا يصدر عنه إلا الواحد يشتمل على مقدمات أخر ضعيفة، وأن الاحتمال والأولوية لا يجدي كثير نفع في المطالب العلمية.
The individual entities are not fit to be parts of the efficient cause; and if they are actual existents, then whether they emanate from the Necessary Being or from the Intellect, it necessarily follows that the One is a source for more than one; likewise if we make the aspects of the Intellect's multiplicity its intellection of necessity and the like. Second: It necessarily follows from what was mentioned that from each intellect there emanates a sphere, a soul, and an intellect ad infinitum, so the intellects are not confined to a number, let alone ten. Third: The statement that the nobler is attributed to the nobler is rhetorical, not befitting demonstrative sciences. Fourth: Attributing the sphere of the fixed stars, despite their multiplicity, to the second intellect by virtue of its possibility establishes the emanation of many from the One; likewise attributing elemental forms and accidents to the last intellect. Fifth: If non-existent aspects and relational aspects were sufficient for the emanation of many from the One, then it would be permissible to attribute it to the Necessary Being by virtue of His negations and relations. Sixth: If the intellects differ in species such that the last is one at which the chain of intellects and spheres terminates—in that no sphere, intellect, or soul emanates from it—then it is possible at the beginning that from the first intellect only a second intellect emanates, and from the second only a third, and so on, until the emanation of the greatest sphere occurs after the emanation of many intellects. In that case, it cannot be definitively asserted that from the first intellect there emanates a sphere, an intellect, and a soul, and that the intellects are ten corresponding to the number of spheres. Moreover, how [can it be] when the partial spheres are many, each requiring a principle? And they admitted that it is possible that between the greatest sphere and the sphere of the fixed stars there are many spheres, and that each of the fixed stars has its own sphere. It is not hidden that their discourse in this context—while founded on the principle that from the One only one proceeds—includes other weak premises, and that probability and preference are of little use in scientific inquiries.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents six objections against the philosophers' theory of emanation, specifically against the principle 'from the One only one proceeds'. The objections are enumerated (second through sixth, with the first being implicit in the opening sentence). Each objection highlights a different logical flaw in the emanationist framework: the impossibility of multiplicity arising from a simple One, the infinite regress of intellects, the rhetorical nature of their assumptions, the inconsistency in attributing multiplicity to lower intellects while denying it to the First, the sufficiency of negations and relations in the Necessary Being, and the arbitrary assumption that the chain ends at ten intellects. The passage concludes by noting that the entire discourse rests on weak premises and that mere probability is insufficient for certain knowledge.

Key Terms
الإمكان
فلك الثوابت
العقل الثاني
الصور
الأعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only the First Intellect can produce multiplicity due to its complexity.
Correction: Sanusi shows that lower intellects also produce multiplicity, contradicting the principle.

Checkpoint
What does the fourth objection use to prove that multiplicity can come from one?
A) The necessity of the First Intellect.
B) The possibility of the second intellect producing many fixed stars.
C) The impossibility of the One producing many.
D) The number of spheres.

Key Takeaway
The fourth objection shows that the philosophers' own attribution of multiplicity to lower intellects contradicts the principle that from one only one proceeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers insisted on a principle ('from one only one proceeds') even as their system contradicted it. Are there beliefs you hold about God's oneness that you might be forced to reconsider if you were honest about the implications of your own actions or thoughts? How will you seek consistency between your theology and your daily practice?
?
The objection reveals that even learned philosophers can fall into logical inconsistency. When you learn a new truth about Allah, such as His absolute independence (al-ghani), does it unsettle you enough to change how you depend on others? What specific attachment will you reexamine today in light of this lesson?

Causality and Created Things

Objection 5: Non-Existent Aspects in the Necessary Being
Fifth objection: negations and relations in God allow multiplicity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth objection: if non-existent aspects (negations and relations) are sufficient to produce multiplicity, then the Necessary Being's own negations and relations would allow multiplicity directly from Him.

Core Idea
God's negations and relations could produce many, too.

The philosophers use non-existent aspects (like possibility) in the lower intellects to explain multiplicity. Sanusi argues that if such non-existents are enough, then the Necessary Being Himself has many negations and relations (e.g., being not composed, being the First, etc.). These would then allow multiplicity to arise directly from God, contradicting the principle and making the emanation chain unnecessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the Fifth Objection
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the terms 'al-haythiyyat al-`adamiyya' (non-existent aspects) and 'al-sulub wa al-idafat' (negations and relations).
2
Understand the Argument by Analogy
If non-existent aspects in the intellects are sufficient to produce multiplicity, then the same should apply to the Necessary Being's negations and relations. But that would mean the One directly produces many, which they deny.
Also, it would eliminate the need for intermediate intellects.
3
Recognize the Implications
This objection shows that the philosophers' reliance on non-existents is ad hoc. The Necessary Being has many negations and relations, so if non-existents count, He should produce multiplicity directly.
This undermines the emanation chain entirely.

Source Text

What does the fifth objection claim about the Necessary Being's negations and relations?

?

?
God's negations and relations are not just theological abstractions — they define your relationship with Him. Are you content to treat His attributes as mere concepts, or do they demand a real transformation in how you worship and obey?
?
If you were to apply the same logical rigor to your own faith that Sanusi applies here, what inconsistencies would you find? Is your belief in God's oneness merely theoretical, or does it shape every decision you make?

Objection 6: Arbitrary Termination of the Chain
Sixth objection: chain is uncertain; weak premises.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth objection: the emanation chain could have taken many forms, and the philosophers' specific claims are not certain; their whole discourse rests on weak premises.

Core Idea
The emanation chain is uncertain and arbitrary.

The sixth objection strikes at the heart of the philosophers' system: if the intellects differ in species, the chain could terminate at any point, not necessarily at ten. Sanusi also notes that there could be many spheres between the greatest sphere and the fixed stars. He concludes that the entire theory is based on weak premises and mere probability, not certainty. This objection comprehensively undermines the emanation model.

Guided Path
1
Read the Sixth Objection
Read the entire Arabic passage for the sixth objection. It is longer and includes the concluding remark. Notice the conditional structure: 'if the intellects differ... then it is possible...'
2
Understand the Conditional Argument
If the last intellect is one that terminates the chain (no sphere, soul, or intellect from it), then the chain could have started differently: from the first intellect only a second, from second only a third, etc., until after many intellects the greatest sphere appears. This would break the fixed pattern of sphere, soul, intellect from each.
3
Note the Admissions
The philosophers themselves admit that there could be many spheres between the greatest sphere and the sphere of the fixed stars, and that each fixed star could have its own sphere. This undermines their numerical claims.
4
Grasp the Final Critique
Sanusi concludes that their discourse includes other weak premises, and that probability and preference (zann and awlawiyya) are insufficient for certain scientific knowledge.
This is a strong methodological criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to the sixth objection, what do the philosophers admit about the spheres?
A) There are exactly ten spheres.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any belief about your faith that you hold simply because it is 'likely' or 'preferred' by scholars, rather than because you have certain knowledge from the Quran and Sunnah? What would it take for you to move from probability to certainty?
?
Sanusi shows that the philosophers admitted possibilities that undermined their entire system. Are you willing to honestly examine your own deeply held convictions, even if they might be weakened? What fear holds you back from such scrutiny?
?
The philosophers relied on weak premises and called it knowledge. In your own life, where have you mistaken probability (e.g., cultural upbringing, personal preference) for certainty about Allah's attributes? How can you purify your knowledge starting today?

The Elemental Mixture of Angels, Jinn, and Devils
Explains elemental composition and predominance for three types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how angels, jinn, and devils are composed from the four elements, with a predominance of fire or air that shapes their nature and abilities.

Core Idea
Elemental predominance determines the subtlety and power of spiritual beings.

This passage delves into the physical composition of angels, jinn, and devils according to the theory of the four elements. It clarifies that while all three are made from earth, water, air, and fire, the predominance of air or fire gives them their subtle and transcendent properties.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on elemental mixture
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall idea. Then read the translation to understand the details of how the three types are composed.
Pay attention to the role of predominance (ghalaba) in determining elemental inclination.
2
Identify the dominant elements
Note that devils are dominated by fire, while angels and jinn are dominated by air. Understand that this dominance affects their substance and abilities.
The passage says 'الغالب على الشياطين عنصر النار، وعلى الآخرين عنصر الهواء'.
3
Understand the variability of predominance
The passage explains that the mixture does not need to be exactly balanced; rather, one element can predominate to varying degrees. This variability accounts for different types of beings.
There is no fixed limit (لا حد معين) for this predominance.
